The Samsung Galaxy Express Prime features 5-inch, Super AMOLED display, Exynos SOC working at 1.3 GHz, 1.5 gigs of RAM and 16GB of expandable internal storage. The phone is powered by 2600 mAh battery and runs Android 6.0. There is 5 megapixel main camera on the back, and 2 megapixel selfie unit in front.. Dimensions: 5.60 x 2.80 x 0.31 inches (142.2 x 71.1 x 7.9 mm). Weight: 4.9 oz (139 g) the average is 5.6 oz (159 g). Resolution: 720 x 1280 pixels. Features: Scratch-resistant glass (Corning Gorilla Glass 4), Ambient light sensor, Proximity sensor. Pixel density - The pixel density of a display represents the number of pixels over an area of one inch. It’s measured in “pixels per inch”, or ppi. The higher the number, the more detailed and good-looking the display is.. Technology - There are two main screen technologies currently used in phones and tablets: LCD and AMOLED. The former usually features a light source and liquid crystals, while the latter is based on organic light-emitting diodes. Newer LCD variations like IPS-LCD and Super-LCD allow for very accurate color reproduction and very wide viewing angles, where no significant image quality loss is observed. Current AMOLED screens differ in such a way that they can exhibit much more saturated colors (sometimes too much) and incredibly high contrast levels, which is due to black color being completely black in AMOLED displays.. Screen-to-body ratio - Shows what part of the frontal area of a phone its screen occupies.. Software Features: Face detection, Digital zoom, Geo tagging. Settings: Exposure compensation, ISO control, White balance presets. Shooting Modes: High Dynamic Range mode (HDR), Panorama, Night mode, Scenes. Aperture size - The aperture of a camera is the opening through which light travels before it reaches the camera sensor. The smaller the number is, the bigger this opening is, allowing for more light to pass.. Quad-core, 1300 MHz, ARM Cortex-A7, 32-bit, 28 nm. System chip - Most modern handsets use an advanced chip that includes many of the device’s hardware modules like the processor, Wi-Fi, Bluetooth and sometimes even the wireless radio. This field shows what particular system chip (or System-on-a-Chip) is used in the phone.. Processor - The processor is the main computing component of a phone and is a major factor when it comes to the overall speed of the device. Some more powerful smartphones use dual-core and quad-core processors designed to deliver greater performance.. Graphics processor - The graphics processor is important for the smooth operation of the system and especially in games and other applications that may involve complex graphics and animations.. System memory - System memory, or RAM memory is the type of memory that the device uses to temporarily store data from the OS or currently-running apps. The more RAM available to the device, the better the performance will be when multiple or heavier programs are running.. Built-in storage - Bigger storage capacity allows you to keep more content saved onto your device, such as more applications, photos or video. Games and video content typically take up the biggest amount of storage space.. Storage expansion - Some handsets allow you to expand their storage capacity by using a memory expansion card – most often microSD. Expansion memory is mostly suitable for media storage, such as photo, video or music content.. Talk time: 22.00 hours the average is 20 h (1229 min). Stand-by time: 10.0 days (240 hours) the average is 21 days (502 h). Capacity - The bigger, the better! However, battery capacity is not the only factor that has an effect on battery life. Those include the chipset in use, the software running on the device, as well as the consumer's unique usage pattern.. Multimedia Screen mirroring: Wireless screen share. Positioning - This field shows the positioning systems supported by the device. The most common types are GPS and A-GPS.. GPS - This is one of the most widespread global positioning technologies, developed and maintained by the U.S. It uses satellites in order to detect your location. A-GPS - A-GPS stands for Assisted GPS and is the industry standard for positioning and navigation. “Assisted” means that it can use local wireless networks, in addition to satellites, for quicker and more precise localization.. Availability Officially announced: 04 Apr 2016. FCC approval - The Federal Communications Commission (FCC) is an independent United States government agency, directly responsible to Congress. The FCC was established by the Communications Act of 1934 and is charged with regulating interstate and international communications by radio, television, wire, satellite and cable. The FCC's jurisdiction covers the 50 states, the District of Columbia, and U.S. Every wireless phone device that is sold in the U.S. has to be tested and approved for sale by the FCC.. Date approved - Shows the date when the particular phone is approved by the Federal Communications Commission. FCC ID value - Shows the FCC Identifying value of the particular phone. FCC measured SAR - Working closely with federal health and safety agencies, such as the Food and Drug Administration (FDA), the FCC has adopted limits for safe exposure to radiofrequency (RF) energy. These limits are given in terms of a unit referred to as the Specific Absorption Rate (SAR), which is a measure of the amount of radio frequency energy absorbed by the body when using a mobile phone. The FCC requires cell phone manufacturers to ensure that their phones comply with these objective limits for safe exposure. Any cell phone at or below these SAR levels (that is, any phone legally sold in the U.S.) is a "safe" phone, as measured by these standards. The FCC limit for public exposure from cellular telephones is an SAR level of 1.6 watts per kilogram (1.6 W/kg).. To see the full specifications with in-depth details click here.. more ... more .... more ... more .... Dimensions 5.60 x 2.80 x 0.31 inches (142.2 x 71.1 x 7.9 mm). Weight 4.9 oz (139 g) the average is 5.6 oz (159 g). Resolution 720 x 1280 pixels. Features Scratch-resistant glass (Corning Gorilla Glass 4), Ambient light sensor, Proximity sensor. Pixel density - The pixel density of a display represents the number of pixels over an area of one inch. It’s measured in “pixels per inch”, or ppi. The higher the number, the more detailed and good-looking the display is.. Technology - There are two main screen technologies currently used in phones and tablets: LCD and AMOLED. The former usually features a light source and liquid crystals, while the latter is based on organic light-emitting diodes. Newer LCD variations like IPS-LCD and Super-LCD allow for very accurate color reproduction and very wide viewing angles, where no significant image quality loss is observed. Current AMOLED screens differ in such a way that they can exhibit much more saturated colors (sometimes too much) and incredibly high contrast levels, which is due to black color being completely black in AMOLED displays.. System chip - Most modern handsets use an advanced chip that includes many of the device’s hardware modules like the processor, Wi-Fi, Bluetooth and sometimes even the wireless radio. This field shows what particular system chip (or System-on-a-Chip) is used in the phone.. Processor - The processor is the main computing component of a phone and is a major factor when it comes to the overall speed of the device. Some more powerful smartphones use dual-core and quad-core processors designed to deliver greater performance.. Graphics processor - The graphics processor is important for the smooth operation of the system and especially in games and other applications that may involve complex graphics and animations.. System memory - System memory, or RAM memory is the type of memory that the device uses to temporarily store data from the OS or currently-running apps. The more RAM available to the device, the better the performance will be when multiple or heavier programs are running.. Built-in storage - Bigger storage capacity allows you to keep more content saved onto your device, such as more applications, photos or video. Games and video content typically take up the biggest amount of storage space.. Storage expansion - Some handsets allow you to expand their storage capacity by using a memory expansion card – most often microSD. Expansion memory is mostly suitable for media storage, such as photo, video or music content.. Talk time 22.00 hours the average is 20 h (1229 min). The most common types are GPS and A-GPS.. GPS - This is one of the most widespread global positioning technologies, developed and maintained by the U.S. It uses satellites in order to detect your location. A-GPS - A-GPS stands for Assisted GPS and is the industry standard for positioning and navigation. “Assisted” means that it can use local wireless networks, in addition to satellites, for quicker and more precise localization.. FCC ID value: A3LSMJ320A link. FCC approval - The Federal Communications Commission (FCC) is an independent United States government agency, directly responsible to Congress. The FCC was established by the Communications Act of 1934 and is charged with regulating interstate and international communications by radio, television, wire, satellite and cable. The FCC's jurisdiction covers the 50 states, the District of Columbia, and U.S. Every wireless phone device that is sold in the U.S. has to be tested and approved for sale by the FCC.. Date approved - Shows the date when the particular phone is approved by the Federal Communications Commission. FCC measured SAR - Working closely with federal health and safety agencies, such as the Food and Drug Administration (FDA), the FCC has adopted limits for safe exposure to radiofrequency (RF) energy. These limits are given in terms of a unit referred to as the Specific Absorption Rate (SAR), which is a measure of the amount of radio frequency energy absorbed by the body when using a mobile phone. The FCC requires cell phone manufacturers to ensure that their phones comply with these objective limits for safe exposure. Any cell phone at or below these SAR levels (that is, any phone legally sold in the U.S.) is a "safe" phone, as measured by these standards. The FCC limit for public exposure from cellular telephones is an SAR level of 1.6 watts per kilogram (1.6 W/kg).. To see the full specifications with in-depth details click here.. Samsung Galaxy Express Prime - Adoptable storage. Float this Topic for Current User. Auto-suggest helps you quickly narrow down your search results by suggesting possible matches as you type.. Samsung Galaxy Express Prime - Adoptable storage. Samsung Galaxy Express Prime - Adoptable storage. I have purchased a Samsung Galaxy Express Prime from the AT&T Store. It is running Android 6 (Marshmallow).. One of the features of Android 6 is "adoptable storage" or being able to use a fast SD card as additional internal storage. (It truly becomes part of the phone storage, and the difference between internal storage and external storage disappears). I'm using a fast SD card that should be able to be adopted, but the option is not showing for me. I'm wondering if it has been disabled in the version of Marshmallow that Samsung is using for the Galaxy Express Prime.. Does anyone have adoptable storage working on a Galaxy Express Prime?. Accepted by topic author bobcrosley. Re: Samsung Galaxy Express Prime - Adoptable storage. Samsung removed the option to enable adoptable storage from the System UI, however there is still a way to enable it. It's a little tricky though, it requires you using Android Debug Bridge (ADB) to configure the SD card for internal storage. This link gives instructions on how to do so (And NO it DOES NOT require you to root your phone). I know it says Galaxy S7 in the link but it works for any Samsung device running Android Marshmallow. My opinion is that Samsung should still have left the option to enable adoptable storage but hid it in the developer options menu.. Accepted by topic author bobcrosley. AT&T Now Offers Galaxy Express Prime, Galaxy Express 3 and Galaxy J3 For GoPhone Customers. 3 April 2016, 10:54 am EDT By Anu Passary Tech Times. Fans of the Samsung Galaxy line-up of smartphones have some exciting news headed their way. network operator AT&T is gearing up to offer the budget-friendly Galaxy Express Prime, Galaxy Express 3 and Galaxy J3 smartphones for customers of its GoPhone.. On Friday, the carrier revealed that it would be retailing the three handsets for GoPhone customers both online and through AT&T's brick and mortar stores.. While the Galaxy Express Prime will go on sale from April 1, GoPhone customers eyeing the Galaxy J3 and Galaxy Express 3 will have to wait another month as they will go on sale from May 6.. "AT&T is continuing to expand its industry leading selection of Samsung devices with a trio of new smartphones. Starting today, you will be able to purchase the Samsung Galaxy Express Prime GoPhone at www.att.com and AT&T stores. Samsung Galaxy J3 and Galaxy Express 3 will be available in the same channels starting May 6," notes. The Galaxy Express 3 and the Galaxy Express Prime are exclusive to AT&T GoPhone.. The entry-level Samsung smartphones are bound to strike a chord with GoPhone customers who are on a budget, but are keen on a robust handset. We take a look at the features and specs of the trio.. The Galaxy Express Prime sports a 5-inch Super AMOLED 720p display. It houses an Exynos 3475 processor and 1.5 GB of RAM. Fueling the smartphone is a 2,600mAh battery. The handset also touts a 5MP primary camera and a 2MP selfie snapper. The Galaxy Express Prime will come with 16 GB of storage and Android 6.0 Marshmallow out of the box.. This handset is the most expensive of the three and costs $129.99. It is available in dark gray. Galaxy Express 3 has a 2,050mAh battery and a 4.5-inch Super AMOLED display, aside from a 5MP rear camera. This smartphone will be available May 6 in white for $79.99.. Smaller than the Galaxy Express Prime, the Galaxy Express 3 has a smaller 4.5-inch Super AMOLED display. The smartphone is fueled by a 2,050mAh battery which offers support for 12 hours of talk time. It also packs in a 5MP primary camera. The smartphone is priced at $79.99 and will retail in white from GoPhone from May 6.. Sporting a 5-inch Super AMOLED 720p screen, this handset houses a Snapdragon 410 quad-core processor clocked at 1.2GHz and 1.5 GB of RAM. It also boasts 16 GB of storage and expandable memory. A 2,600mAh battery powers the Galaxy J3 which will be available in white for GoPhone customers from May 6.. The Galaxy J3 starts at $5.67 per month (for 30 months) as part of the Next24 Plan.. AT&T Announces The GoPhone-Exclusive Galaxy Express Prime And Galaxy Express 3, Along With The KNOX-Equipped Galaxy J3. 2016/04/01 11:35am PST Apr 1, 2016. The high-end of the market attracts all the fame and glory, but millions of people are carrying around prepaid low-end phones in their pockets. And these days, the low-end of the market isn't what it used to be. Android enthusiasts will know that phone you pulled out isn't top-of-the-line, but the average person will think that 5-inch 720p display looks pretty snazzy.. AT&T is introducing two new Galaxy phones for its GoPhone line. One, the Samsung Galaxy Express Prime, is available starting today for $129.99 .. $129.99 is the full price you pay for the aforementioned screen, an Exynos 3475 processor, 1.5GB of RAM, a 2600mAh battery, 5MP/2MP cameras, and 16GB of internal storage (along with a microSD card slot). It's not the worse way to get a taste of Android 6.0, which you may not have experienced yet if you're carrying around a low-end phone from last year.. The Galaxy Express Prime is hardly priced as low as phones can go. To attract buyers who are even more frugal with their money, the company will also release the Express 3, a $79.99 phone with a smaller 4.5-inch display and 2050mAh battery. It will become available through GoPhone on May 6th.. On that same day, AT&T also plans to release the Galaxy J3, a non-GoPhone device that will cost $5.67 a month with a Next 24 plan. This handset is geared for business use due to Samsung KNOX support. Expect more information early next month.. Trio of Samsung Smartphones Available to AT&T Customers Beginning April 1. Prepaid, Postpaid Samsung Smartphones with Marshmallow Available Nationwide this Spring. AT&T* is continuing to expand its industry leading selection of Samsung devices with a trio of new smartphones. Starting today, you will be able to purchase the Samsung Galaxy Express Prime GoPhone at www.att.com and AT&T stores. Samsung Galaxy J3 and Galaxy Express 3 will be available in the same channels starting May 6.. Available exclusively with AT&T, the Galaxy Express Prime GoPhone features the latest Android Marshmallow operating system and a 2600mAh battery, so you can move between your favorite apps quickly and easily throughout the day. Enjoy an enhanced video viewing experience with Galaxy Express Prime’s 5 inch Super AMOLED display. Additionally, the phone’s Easy Mode lets you customize your home screen to your personal preferences with larger, easier to read icons.. The Galaxy Express Prime GoPhone is available exclusively at AT&T for $129.99 in dark gray.. Samsung Galaxy Express 3 features a 4.5 inch Super AMOLED display. It has a 2050mAh battery that provides talk time for up to 12 hours.1 Additionally, the Galaxy Express 3 has a 5 megapixel rear-facing camera that allows you to easily take candid photos.. The Galaxy Express 3 is available exclusively through GoPhone in white for $79.99.. The Samsung Galaxy J3 keeps you connected, entertained and in-the-loop with your friends, family and co-workers. There is ample room to store your favorite pictures and music, with the Galaxy J3 having up to 16GB of built-in memory.2 You can expand your device storage up to 128GB with a microSD card (sold separately).. The Galaxy J3 also provides security for your business at a value that lets you equip your entire workforce with an affordable and smart device.. The Galaxy J3 enables 256 bit encryption by default, and with Samsung KNOX support there is built in defense grade security at the hardware level.. Using an EMM solution, the Galaxy J3 can be managed and protected at a high level.. Pricing for the Galaxy J3 starts at $5.67 per month for 30 months for well qualified customers on AT&T Next 24.3 The Galaxy J3 is available in white.. For more information, check out www.att.com.. *AT&T products and services are provided or offered by subsidiaries and affiliates of AT&T Inc. under the AT&T brand and not by AT&T Inc.. AT&T picks up affordable Galaxy Express Prime, Express 3 and J3 Marshmallow phones. Adrian Diaconescu April 4, 2016 6:01 am. It took far longer than we had wished and expected, but finally, Android 6.0 software goodies are becoming the norm instead of the exception for even low-cost new devices.. Case in point, a trio of prepaid and postpaid smartphones sold by AT&T for less than $200 apiece. One model is available already through the nation’s second largest carrier both on and offline, while the other two will barely roll out on May 6 for reasons we don’t fully understand.. Perhaps their Marshmallow ports aren’t ready for primetime yet, as the Galaxy J3 first landed on Boost and Virgin Mobile back in January with Lollipop pre-loaded.. But let’s start from the beginning. The Samsung Galaxy Express Prime can be purchased today on GoPhone prepaid plans at $130. If the release timing didn’t give it away, this looks identical to Cricket’s Galaxy Amp Prime , with the same physical home key and duo of adjoining capacitive buttons in tow, a 5-inch 720p Super AMOLED display, and 5 and 2MP cameras.. There’s also 4G LTE connectivity on deck, 16GB expandable storage, and a 2,600 mAh removable battery. Overall, not a bad quality – pricing ratio.. The $80 Samsung Galaxy Express 3 likely provides enough bang as well, featuring a 4.5-inch AMOLED screen, 2,050 mAh cell, and 5MP rear-facing snapper.. Finally, the Galaxy J3 or J3 (2016) will be sold on Next 24 payment plans for $5.67 a month, the 30 installments resulting in a grand total of $170. You’re probably looking at a J3 variant with 8 and 5MP cams ergo, plus 1.5GB RAM, quad-core power, 2,600 mAh juice, and LTE network speeds..
